<div id="review_1404973296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1404973296" />
    <a title="Douglas Milewski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18815007-douglas-milewski"><img alt="Douglas Milewski" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477525827p2/18815007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1404973296?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Douglas Milewski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Douglas Milewski" href="/user/show/18815007-douglas-milewski">Douglas Milewski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739407004" href="/book/show/61996.The_First_Chronicles_of_Amber">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1404973296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6500673790913361078">The First Chronicles of Amber were like nothing in the 1970's fantasy market, and they've pretty much stayed their way. More a serial than a novel, the book follows the "adventures" of Lord Corwin, a prince of Amber, the only "real" place in the world. With no irony, this was the original game of thrones.<br/><br/>These books aren't refined literature. The sentences are not pretty. The sentiments are not politically correct. The prose has all the refinement of 50 grit sandpaper. If you like quality prose,</span>
  <span id="freeText6500673790913361078" style="display:none">The First Chronicles of Amber were like nothing in the 1970's fantasy market, and they've pretty much stayed their way. More a serial than a novel, the book follows the "adventures" of Lord Corwin, a prince of Amber, the only "real" place in the world. With no irony, this was the original game of thrones.<br /><br />These books aren't refined literature. The sentences are not pretty. The sentiments are not politically correct. The prose has all the refinement of 50 grit sandpaper. If you like quality prose, skip this book. You'll never be happy. The prose here is serviceable, but no more than serviceable. This is a book written for the mass market, a power fantasy for the train riding office worker. Your enemies and your allies are the same people, and everyone has the same goal: take the big chair for themselves. Yet, not everyone can take that chair. Alliances are made and broken at a fast pace. Everyone lies. Retconning in this book rises to the level of art.<br /><br />Yet, despite its flaws, the work is fascinating. When I say it's a power fantasy, we're talking people akin to gods fighting for the rulership of the magical universe. Magic is interesting without descending into system dinkage. Great power always remains dangerous enough to give everyone second thoughts. And the end is most certainly not predictable from the beginning. This thing has more twists and turns than the pattern itself.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6500673790913361078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_11774808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11774808" />
    <a title="Radu Stanculescu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/748293-radu-stanculescu"><img alt="Radu Stanculescu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432030977p2/748293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11774808?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Radu Stanculescu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Radu Stanculescu" href="/user/show/748293-radu-stanculescu">Radu Stanculescu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/748293-radu-stanculescu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/748293-radu-stanculescu?shelf=cluj">cluj</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11774808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3244143747647230383">This is one of the most "realistic" fantasy series I've read - admittedly, I haven't read that much fantasy, but still. The power struggle that goes on throughout the series could easily be one from a more "down-to-earth" society, and the fantastic elements only serve to augment the story, without overwhelming it. The characters' actions and motivation are strikingly human, and you won't find the classical "good guy/bad guy" distinction you find in many fantasy books; everybody has their shade o</span>
  <span id="freeText3244143747647230383" style="display:none">This is one of the most "realistic" fantasy series I've read - admittedly, I haven't read that much fantasy, but still. The power struggle that goes on throughout the series could easily be one from a more "down-to-earth" society, and the fantastic elements only serve to augment the story, without overwhelming it. The characters' actions and motivation are strikingly human, and you won't find the classical "good guy/bad guy" distinction you find in many fantasy books; everybody has their shade of grey, and you'll learn to understand if not accept their decisions.<br /><br />Thinking a bit more about this, I remember how I felt throughout Corwin's transformation. The story being written in first person he was of course a hero to himself and his enemies were wrong all the time in the first book. Later in the series though he starts to understand that some of the perceived differences between him and his rivals were merely caused by his ambitions being mirrored in others. And it turned out that some of the "evil" things done against him were not so evil after all. I think this kind of "waking up" is difficult to portray in a series/book, even more when you only have one point of view to work with, and that's the person waking up. And Zelazny has done it brilliantly.<br /><br />Maybe it's time I read this again. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3244143747647230383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164638459?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/5350919-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575082694" href="/book/show/3408137-chronicles-of-amber">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5350919-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164638459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13724180071424344841"> The Chronicles of Amber is a beautifully written fantasy series containing magic, epic battles, court politics and the occasional fratricide. However, this is not fantasy in the traditional sense; at times this reads as a crime thriller or murder mystery, where one has to solve the clues together to work out the culprit. Through this style of writing, Zelazny weaves together a complex narrative told from the perspective of Prince Corwin of Amber, one of nine brothers vying to claim the throne o</span>
  <span id="freeText13724180071424344841" style="display:none"> The Chronicles of Amber is a beautifully written fantasy series containing magic, epic battles, court politics and the occasional fratricide. However, this is not fantasy in the traditional sense; at times this reads as a crime thriller or murder mystery, where one has to solve the clues together to work out the culprit. Through this style of writing, Zelazny weaves together a complex narrative told from the perspective of Prince Corwin of Amber, one of nine brothers vying to claim the throne of Amber, all of whom believe they have a legitimate claim.<br /> This is a fast paced, character-driven series full of intrigue and suspense. Zelazny brings a level of detail to his world of which most authors can only dream, and he populates this richly imagined land with an array of scheming, conniving, Machiavellian characters to boot. Each brothers' charismatic personality oozes from the page, drawing the reader in, and I had better not forget to mention the four sisters and the mad mage with dangerous powers, each with their own secret ambitions and allegiances.<br /> If you are looking for something beyond the traditional fantasy then look no further, this series will capture your imagination and turn it on its head.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13724180071424344841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10110379-caroline-berg?shelf=all-about-revenge">all-about-revenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10110379-caroline-berg?shelf=magic-users">magic-users</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345572255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17463036749702576753">My only regret is that I didn't read these books sooner. These first five books are wonderful - I would rate them five stars each. The action is non-stop. The intrigue changes so many times it is hard to keep track of who is allied with whom. It can be fatal to trust the wrong person - but who can you trust when your entire family is locked in a battle for the throne? Relatives pop out of the woodwork like termites - but do they want the throne, revenge or something else? Nothing is ever what it</span>
  <span id="freeText17463036749702576753" style="display:none">My only regret is that I didn't read these books sooner. These first five books are wonderful - I would rate them five stars each. The action is non-stop. The intrigue changes so many times it is hard to keep track of who is allied with whom. It can be fatal to trust the wrong person - but who can you trust when your entire family is locked in a battle for the throne? Relatives pop out of the woodwork like termites - but do they want the throne, revenge or something else? Nothing is ever what it seems. The first book of the series, Nine Princes in Amber, was brilliantly done. It starts with Corey not remembering anything. So as he struggles to find out what is going on, the reader learns with him. The first book also ends with a cliff-hanger, so naturally, now you have to read the next book... and so on until you realize that you have now read them all.<br /><br />These books are classic, not to mention necessary, if you ever want to play Amber Diceless Roleplaying - or get any Amber references in any other fantasy games. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17463036749702576753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_622999222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622999222" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7460078-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423057907p2/7460078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622999222?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/7460078-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622999222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16339537946050122297">Excellent series with infinite universes, quarreling Gods, and crazy plot twists. The writing is minimalistic and reads sort of like Hemingway crossed with a 1940s detective novel, except with random Shakespeare quotations thrown everywhere. The character of Corwin really grows on the reader and shifts from a machiavellian royal to an enjoyable protagonist. At first Corwin is someone who is willing to kill his own sibling and send thousands of men he has duped to their deaths in order to get the</span>
  <span id="freeText16339537946050122297" style="display:none">Excellent series with infinite universes, quarreling Gods, and crazy plot twists. The writing is minimalistic and reads sort of like Hemingway crossed with a 1940s detective novel, except with random Shakespeare quotations thrown everywhere. The character of Corwin really grows on the reader and shifts from a machiavellian royal to an enjoyable protagonist. At first Corwin is someone who is willing to kill his own sibling and send thousands of men he has duped to their deaths in order to get the crown. He may remind readers of Game of Thrones somewhat of Stannis Baratheon. Later Corwin shows that he cares for the realm and not just gaining power. Corwin is willing to risk his life and even sacrifice it for the greater good of Amber. The story is told from Corwin's perspective so he is by far the most fleshed out character, but other characters are amusing as well. There is the badass Benedict, strong and dumb Gerard, the hilarious Random, and plenty of others. Overall this is a series worth reading for anyone who enjoys fantasy literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16339537946050122297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Zack Stackurski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18804994-zack-stackurski"><img alt="Zack Stackurski" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370700663p2/18804994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/573266629?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zack Stackurski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zack Stackurski" href="/user/show/18804994-zack-stackurski">Zack Stackurski</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573266629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9484965625792076092">I think the Chronicles of Amber are a lot of fun... and certainly very different. Zelazny's schtik is explaining how magic works in an almost science fictiony sort of way. He doesn't go that far in this one... but the reality bending powers of the Amberites are fun and different all the same. Even better, the series starts out almost like a mystery as the amnesiatic character tries to figure out who and what the heck he really is. This leads to a pretty epic tale of betrayal and family infightin</span>
  <span id="freeText9484965625792076092" style="display:none">I think the Chronicles of Amber are a lot of fun... and certainly very different. Zelazny's schtik is explaining how magic works in an almost science fictiony sort of way. He doesn't go that far in this one... but the reality bending powers of the Amberites are fun and different all the same. Even better, the series starts out almost like a mystery as the amnesiatic character tries to figure out who and what the heck he really is. This leads to a pretty epic tale of betrayal and family infighting... but the battle that ends the book leaves things feeling a bit unfinished. It still feels like a complete tale all the same though and I think an unfinished ending does such a malleable story justice. I know there is a second Chronicle I should probably read to see what other sorts of stories Zelazny dreamed up in Amber...</span>

It took me a very long time to sit down and start it, but that happens with most of the books I read as a rule it seems. He gave it to me with the promise that these books changed his life. As of this point, I find them AMAZING! the descriptions are beautiful and the plot is enticing. It continues to build and draw you in in what I suspect as a calculated way. I've also suggested the series to 3 other Sci-Fi readers who report to me with enthusiasm how much they are enjoying the stories. <br />I began my more involved reading with the Sci-fi genre, but now tend towards very different interests, but I can't help but love this story.</span>

  <span id="freeText3622155865273576435" style="display:none">Well, I went and did it. You have my report on "Nine Princes in Amber". Since I had the rest of the book, which is the entire Corwin series, and a little time I thought I'd taste the second book. That was a huge mistake, I was hooked, and now, 600 pages later I am left with the problem of reviewing it. As the hero travels through reality and shadow where anything can and does happen ( Corwin meets the book's author on page 502) the saga can hardly be described by anything shorter than itself.<br /><br />In the last book, "The Courts of Chaos", Zelazny finally goes full,bull goose, Lewis Carroll on us and the parallels to that classic become apparent. <div id="review_2867974401" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2867974401" />

<span id="freeTextContainer957094399232108653">Amazing world. Multitude of world you can dive head first, to be correct. Curious and non-conventional world building and magical system. I think of Amber as a standart for all fantasy worlds. You read and believe that that can be true for real. Magic acts according to clearly defined rules. Jumps from a world to a world. And a path of a protagonist feels real. He is growing and changing from one book to another. I can recommend Amber Chronicles as an outstanding epic fantasy.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pikADniK1+0Q0bPfe23n4CVNSc7Nyd/jQj8SlJezRiUwXHPU75hUo/JhxnE8o8TaWf+nogFZ/vh3G3BkpxOJpQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hQG/cw2vJeHD8uxfoMyxgKfuNnS2ILedpIqmtVMROBkTdMypmr2mryFCmfHnApK621zYGHqwloaRrsRFY7H3mQ==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_19898'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19898.Assembling_California?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Assembling California<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/40.John_McPhee?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">John McPhee<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.17 avg rating &mdash; 1,772 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1992\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer10321571819500129629\">At various times in a span of fifteen years, John McPhee made geological field surveys in the company of Eldridge Moores, a tectonicist at the University of California at Davis. The result of these trips is Assembling California, a cross-section in h<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10321571819500129629\" style=\"display:none\">At various times in a span of fifteen years, John McPhee made geological field surveys in the company of Eldridge Moores, a tectonicist at the University of California at Davis. The result of these trips is Assembling California, a cross-section in human and geologic time, from Donner Pass in the Sierra Nevada through the golden foothills of the Mother Lode and across the Great Central Valley to the wine country of the Coast Ranges, the rock of San Francisco, and the San Andreas family of faults. The two disparate time scales occasionally intersect--in the gold disruptions of the nineteenth century no less than in the earthquakes of the twentieth--and always with relevance to a newly understood geologic history in which half a dozen large and separate pieces of country are seen to have drifted in from far and near to coalesce as California.\n\nMcPhee and Moores also journeyed to remote mountains of Arizona and to Cyprus and northern Greece, where rock of the deep-ocean floor has been transported into continental settings, as it has in California.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny">About Roger Zelazny</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207671346p3/3619.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny">Roger Zelazny
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,062
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9252668883791048926">Roger Zelazny made his name with a group of novellas which demonstrated just how intense an emotional charge could be generated by the stock imagery of sf; the most famous of these is <i>A Rose for Ecclesiastes</i> in which a poet struggles to convince dying and sterile Martians that life is worth continuing. Zelazny continued to write excellent short stories throughout his career. Most of his novels dea</span>
  <span id="freeText9252668883791048926" style="display:none">Roger Zelazny made his name with a group of novellas which demonstrated just how intense an emotional charge could be generated by the stock imagery of sf; the most famous of these is <i>A Rose for Ecclesiastes</i> in which a poet struggles to convince dying and sterile Martians that life is worth continuing. Zelazny continued to write excellent short stories throughout his career. Most of his novels deal, one way or another, with tricksters and mythology, often with rogues who become gods, like Sam in <i>Lord of Light</i>, who reinvents Buddhism as a vehicle for political subversion on a colony planet.<br /><br />The fantasy sequence <i>The Amber Chronicles</i>, which started with <i>Nine Princes in Amber</i>, deals with the ruling family of a Platonic realm at the metaphysical heart of things, who can slide, trickster-like through realities, and their wars with each other and the related ruling house of Chaos. Zelazny never entirely fulfilled his early promise—who could?—but he and his work were much loved, and a potent influence on such younger writers as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R__R__Martin" title="George R. R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R. R. Martin</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a>.<br /><br />He won the Nebula award three times (out of 14 nominations) and the Hugo award six times (out of 14 nominations). His <a href="http://aok.lib.umbc.edu/specoll/Zelazny/index.php" rel="nofollow noopener">papers are housed</a> at the Albin O. Khun Library of the University of Maryland, Baltimore County (UMBC).<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Zelazny">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Ze...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9252668883791048926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
